This review is specifically for Ms Jezebel. I have not tried any of the other escape rooms at this location. This was my 5th or 6th escape room experience and my first escape room with a live person(I heard there are few other escape rooms like that). It's very different from your other escape rooms. It's like watching theater/show but you get to be part of it! In addition to solving puzzles, you really feel like you are a cast in a murder mystery dinner show.

Our Ms. Jezebel was played by Dorothy. She was an amazing actress! I don't want to say much else cause I don't want to give our spoilers...but she made it super fun.

I think it adds a new and exciting touch to the escape room experience.<//Text>

< review>
I've done 2 out of 3 rooms at this location and have been impressed by the creativity and attention to detail in both Ms. Jezebel and Tiki time.

Both are novel takes on escape rooms; Jezebel in particular was a one-of-a-kind experience that I've never seen in the 70+ escape rooms that I've done.

Our GM Patrick was spectacular in the titular role of Jezebel and was a big part in what made the room so incredible. I'm sure the other GMs are also phenomenal as well, but kudos to Patrick for making our night so wonderful!

Tiki time was also great. The room is packed with puzzles and things to do, and the atmosphere and set design was wonderfully immersive.

This location also has plenty of on-site parking which makes it infinitely more convinient than other rooms in L.A. that may require tricky street parking.</review>

<Review>The Service: Very friendly staffs~ Gave us very detail instructions how the game works. We are one of the testing groups and they monitor us through out the game. When they saw us struggling, they would come in the room and give us some hints. They are definitely want to improve the games and make it more challenging and entertaining.

The Game: 45 minutes to find the key and get out the room.... shouldn't be too hard right? WRONG!! This is the time you really really really have to THINK!! Everything in the room can be clues. Love the timer on the big screen TV.... made your heart pounds so fast! We want to escape!

This is a great outing with your family and friends. You can have maximum 10 people per room. It is all about TEAMWORK, people!! If you like to be challenge and love to work under pressure, this is definitely the game for you.

<Time>1573432302250</Time><Rating>5< /Rating><review>I've done over 125 escape rooms in Seattle, LA, New Orleans, Houston, and the Bay Area. I actively travel and seek out the best escape rooms in the US, so this review is catered specifically to enthusiasts looking for unique, high quality rooms.

Miss Jezebel - mid 4/5 | Rank 34/145 (Good room with a little something that makes the room distinctive. We will happily recommend these rooms to travelling enthusiasts or locals.)

Miss Jezebel is something like 75% immersive theatre, and 25% escape room. This is probably the first room of this type that we‚Äôve played: Strange Bird in Houston is the other immersive theatre room that comes to mind, but that was more of an immersive theater intro/outro sandwiched by a standard 60 minute escape room. In this room, the game consists almost entirely of interacting with the live actor in the room  (Patrick was great) with a little bit of improv (but it‚Äôs easy improv since it‚Äôs very obvious what you‚Äôre supposed to say/do), with some breaks so that you can do some old fashion escape rooming. The game is advertised as ‚Äúraunchy‚Äù, which means that theres some kinky adult subject matter in the room, and you may have to embarrass yourself by doing certain things. These things aren‚Äôt anything beyond PG-13 and pretty tame so don‚Äôt worry about that, but you probably don‚Äôt want to do this room if you take yourself super seriously.

We personally really enjoyed this room and think it‚Äôs unique enough to check out even for enthusiasts who have done a ton of rooms, and thought it was a fresh take on the escape room genre. Spending almost the entire time interacting with the actor was pretty fun even for someone not as sociable like me, and if you‚Äôre into comedy/a little bit of improv, you‚Äôll probably have a blast trying to figure out who this Jezebel person really is. I would not recommend this room if you mainly like puzzles or find interacting with people troublesome (though the actor does a pretty good job at reading how into this you are and will probably act accordingly) - the puzzles in the room are pretty basic, and the enjoyment of the room is dependent entirely on you thinking that interacting with the actor is fun (which most people will probably think is fun).

Set - The set is a bit small, but does a good job for the purposes of the game, which is giving you a creepy apartment to work with while you interact with Jezebel. The ambiance is good, there‚Äôs some surprises, and it‚Äôs generally pretty functional despite most of it being non-interactive.

Story - The overall story is fairly simple (collect evidence vs Jezebel) and is pretty straightforward, the interactions with Jezebel and attempting to have a tea party with her are hilarious and involves some strange and interesting sequences. You‚Äôll need to perform a bunch of simple but funny tasks in order to appease Jezebel, and the conclusion is quite dramatic. There was a ton of story content here in the interactions, and throughout the room I felt like I eventually gained a sense of camraderie with Jezebel, since even though she was crazy, we had some pretty good times together.

Puzzles -There wasn‚Äôt a ton of puzzling in this room (maybe 5 or so), and they were all generally pretty simple. Not really the focus of the room, but that‚Äôs fine. Some of the puzzles were funny social engineering puzzles where you had to figure out how to do something while not attracting the attention of Jezebel - this was generally pretty easy, but still felt thrilling since there was always the uncertainty of whether or not Jezebel would catch you. There was also a good amount of humor injected into the puzzles which was fun, and one particular puzzle was hilarious in that regard.</review><pictures>None</pictures>< resp>
None< /resp>

My group and I have done quite a few escape rooms in the LA area, and so far this is definitely one of our top experiences. My only criticism is that in a large group like ours, not everyone is able to be involved with each part of the puzzle, and so it would have been really nice if the room facilitator actually took time after we escaped to recap what happened. As it was, we felt sort of rushed out, without any real time to talk about what happened. But the puzzles were thoughtful and intricate, the mechanics were awesome (it seemed like things happened by magic!) and we were definitely challenged at a good level. Overall a great experience.<//Text>

thoroughly enjoyed myself here. Countdown Live is located super close to the convention center and if you blink your eye, you might just miss this hot spot.
Free PARKING ! A major perk and unheard of especially in downtown la!

Countdown Live has a total of 3 rooms, Tiki, ( the hardest and biggest room that holds a total of 10 people comfortably) Spaceship, (their most newest room) and Psycho, which is going to be revamp very soon!

I chose the Psycho room with 35% success rate of passing and supposedly the easiest. I enjoy the scary theme as I was barely getting over Halloween. Psycho truly gave us a few screams. I am not going to ruin anything for the rest of you but def. brought out the goose bumps!

I highly recommend paying them a visit!<//text>

< review>
I just played the Krampus Room a few hours ago, and I can't stop thinking about it. It was absolutely amazing! When it comes to horror escape rooms I've found that most are either all scare and no puzzles, or all puzzles and no scare. Krampus does a masterful job of showcasing both. The puzzles were interesting, intuitive, and at times pretty difficult with a good combo of more traditional locks and high tech puzzles. At the same time, I was in a constant state of unease throughout the experience and there was more than a few times when that unease quickly evolved into outright terror. Krampus is pretty high ranking in the best escape rooms I've ever played, and it personally takes my #1 spot for horror rooms specifically. Excited to see what else Countdown has in store!<//review>

This is probably one of my favorite Boba places in the bay area for the quality of the drinks, food, and overall atmosphere.

What I like:
- Open relatively late for the area (11p)
- Free WiFi
- Good drinks
- Delicious popcorn chicken
- Plenty of seating with couches for groups

<user_id>113294607675859396808<//user_id><user_name>Kevin Luck</user_name><Time>1422589879456<//Time><rating>5<//rating>< Text>
Exceptional!

This is one of those small places that you feel you must write about to give them their due, but you hate to tune in more people to this place because they are already packed for business. But alas, must do the right thing...

The food here was absolutely incredible - top to bottom. I thought I was at the CIA (culinary institute) having dinner. It just had those perfect chef touches on each dish.

We had several of the tapas plates for appetizers and the the main meal. I enjoyed the Steak Frites with a juicy, perfectly trimmed and cooked Sirloin. My wife had the special which was fish and said it was amazing.

Very good wine menu to accompany the food with a nice bar area that fills up quickly.

Just know, if you go on the weekend after 6, you will be waiting outside for a table for awhile. It's unfortunate but speaks to how good this place is.< /Text>

< Review>
Every time we visit the Black Trumpet we are never disappointed.  Never mind that the menu is crafted by one of the great chefs here in America, if not beyond, Dino. He's always available and will often come and say hello and shake your hand. That's when you get the opportunity to share with him how perfect his food is and how wonderful are his staff. They don't take reservations and they are open for lunch too. They have an extensive wine list as they are a wine bar and now they will be serving mixed cocktails. We stumbled upon this great Bistro a couple of years ago before it made its move to Seacliff Village. I believe we have been there at least 12 or 15 times. Always a great evening without exception! We always have the clam and mussel appetizer with the smoked French bread that is toasted, it is hard to describe how delicious is this dish. This last visit my husband had the Coltrane which is a filet mignon with french fries and as usual it was flavorful, tender, and a large portion. I tried something new as I was hungry for rotisserie chicken. The Cornish game hen was unbelievably savory tender and with perfect and crispy skin. Served with saffron pilaf and mixed vegetables including asparagus. The handcrafted fair at this restaurant is beyond five stars and consistent. The ambiance in their new location is also like an exciting French bistro. There is an outdoor patio with a fire pit or indoor dining where you feel as if you're in a French nightclub. We love sitting at the bar or at the open kitchen where the chefs are always friendly and love to entertain. I can't say enough about this extraordinary  gem in Huntington Beach. Romantic, comfortable, inviting and you always feel like you've arrived at a family home restaurant.  Plenty of parking and wheel chair accessible. Don't miss this one for a wonderful occasion or just a date night out!</Review>

< text>
Came here on a Friday evening with a small group of friends after a glowing recommendation from a friend.

The ambiance was super cute. It's a very small and cozy restaurant, but what i loved most was how the service never felt rushed and attention to detail! They have an amazing wine list to compliment their extensive menu. The menu is definitely both veg and non-veg friendly which was a huge win for our party.

While they are a small restaurant, expect to wait and enjoy a glass of wine from their bar. They also do not take reservations.

For dinner, we shared family style and ordered numerous items. Items included:
- Baked Brie
- Truffle Fries
- Daily Special (Eggplant Parmesan)
- Daily Special (Lamb Kebobs)
- Brussels Sprouts w/ chorizo o the side
- Fig Pizza

Everything turned out AMAZING! The food comes out as plates are hot and ready, so don't expect this to all come out at once. Definitely more of the tapas style.

Overall, amazing food, wine selection and dessert selection! So glad we finally came here and will definitely be back again for more food soon!!</text>

<Review>At first glance, this restaurant's interior doesn't say much but once you enter you'll be surprised by how busy it is.

I was casually looking for a place to eat for date night and found this restaurant black trumpet bistro.

Interior decor looks nice. Very much like a nice bistro.  We were seated on chef's table because it was so busy.  Chef's table - there you can see them at work making your meal.  They were fast in getting our appetizers and entrees out.

I don't think the truffle fries were worth it.  There was no flavor in the fries and tasted more like garlic fries.  Duck breast appetizer was totally worth it.  The right amount of fat and protein.  Tasty!

Had lamb shank and it was ok.  I thought it was a little too salty but otherwise it was very tender.  Figs were a nice touch.  I've never had figs with my entree before.

Fiance had kabob.  At first he was worried one stick of steak kabob was not enough but actually it worked with w the veggie kabob and the meat chunks was pretty big.

Overall it's a nice place to check out.  Will recommend people to come a little early for better seating.</Review><Pics>None<//Pics><Resp>None<//Resp><gmapID>0x80dd26c3c1507f5d:0x177ef0d65f0ea6a5<//gmapID></record>

A delightful, dim, and romantic little bistro that serves up the most amazing tapas dishes alongside 1950's jazz. Wanda Harlowe< /user_name>
<time>1487640664936<//time><rate>5<//rate>< Text>
Whether you're a resident Los Angelo or a visitor to the City of Angels, the French Florist should be your "go-to" place should you desire vibrant, custom designed floral arrangements that are second to none in the design genre.

The owner's, Steve and Angela, along with their talented troop of designers and ever multi-tasking diligent staff are always, or so it seems, going far and above the call to surpass the expectations of their expansive and ever growing clientele.

If you are new to the area or visiting and need to make a unique expression, thought or thank you to a special someone, the team at this long established shop will create the awe you want manifested.

Walk-in's are welcome, however free parking is limited and street slots are metered, so I'd suggest a combination of calling and Internet communication first.

Major credit cards accepted, along with regular and express delivery options are available.
